Task instruction sent to agent 
# Task: Implement CompactDiffFormatter for Terraform

## Objective
Create a `CompactDiffFormatter` in `internal/command/format/` that produces a condensed,
summary-style diff output for `terraform plan`, showing only resource-level changes
without attribute-level detail.

## Requirements

1. **Create `internal/command/format/compact.go`** with:
   - `CompactDiffFormatter` struct implementing a plan formatter
   - `Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *terraform.Schemas)` method returning string
   - Outputs one line per resource change: `[action] resource_type.name`
   - Groups changes by action type (create/update/delete/replace)
   - Shows summary counts at the end

2. **Create `internal/command/format/compact_test.go`** with tests

3. **Follow Terraform patterns**:
   - Study the existing `DiffFormatter` in the format package
   - Use `plans.Action` constants (Create, Update, Delete, etc.)
   - Use `addrs.AbsResourceInstance` for resource addressing

## Key Reference Files
- `internal/command/format/diff.go` — existing diff formatter
- `internal/command/format/state.go` — state formatter pattern
- `internal/plans/changes.go` — plan change types
- `internal/plans/plan.go` — Plan struct definition
- `internal/addrs/resource.go` — resource addressing

## Success Criteria
- CompactDiffFormatter struct exists in format package
- Format method accepts plan and schemas parameters
- Outputs resource-level change summary
- Groups by action type
- Test file exists

     4→// Package format contains helpers for formatting various Terraform
     5→// structures for human-readabout output.
     6→//
     7→// This package is used by the official Terraform CLI in formatting any
     8→// output and is exported to encourage non-official frontends to mimic the
     9→// output formatting as much as possible so that text formats of Terraform
    10→// structures have a consistent look and feel.
    11→package format
    12→
    13→import "github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
    14→
    15→// DiffActionSymbol returns a string that, once passed through a
    16→// colorstring.Colorize, will produce a result that can be written
    17→// to a terminal to produce a symbol made of three printable
    18→// characters, possibly interspersed with VT100 color codes.
    19→func DiffActionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {
    20→	switch action {
    21→	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
    22→		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset]"
    23→	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
    24→		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset]"
    25→	case plans.Create:
    26→		return "  [green]+[reset]"
    27→	case plans.Delete:
    28→		return "  [red]-[reset]"
    29→	case plans.Forget:
    30→		return " [red].[reset]"
    31→	case plans.CreateThenForget:
    32→		return " [green]+[reset]/[red].[reset]"
    33→	case plans.Read:
    34→		return " [cyan]<=[reset]"
    35→	case plans.Update:
    36→		return "  [yellow]~[reset]"
    37→	case plans.NoOp:
    38→		return "   "
    39→	default:
    40→		return "  ?"
    41→	}
    42→}
    43→

     4→package plans
     5→
     6→type Action rune
     7→
     8→const (
     9→	NoOp             Action = 0
    10→	Create           Action = '+'
    11→	Read             Action = '←'
    12→	Update           Action = '~'
    13→	DeleteThenCreate Action = '∓'
    14→	CreateThenDelete Action = '±'
    15→	Delete           Action = '-'
    16→	Forget           Action = '.'
    17→	CreateThenForget Action = '⨥'
    18→	Open             Action = '⟃'
    19→	Renew            Action = '⟳'
    20→	Close            Action = '⫏'
    21→)
    22→
    23→//go:generate go run golang.org/x/tools/cmd/stringer -type Action
    24→
    25→// IsReplace returns true if the action is one of the actions that
    26→// represent replacing an existing object with a new object.
    27→func (a Action) IsReplace() bool {
    28→	return a == DeleteThenCreate || a == CreateThenDelete || a == CreateThenForget
    29→}

    14→// Resource is an address for a resource block within configuration, which
    15→// contains potentially-multiple resource instances if that configuration
    16→// block uses "count" or "for_each".
    17→type Resource struct {
    18→	referenceable
    19→	Mode ResourceMode
    20→	Type string
    21→	Name string
    22→}
    23→
    24→func (r Resource) String() string {
    25→	switch r.Mode {
    26→	case ManagedResourceMode:
    27→		return fmt.Sprintf("%s.%s", r.Type, r.Name)
    28→	case DataResourceMode:
    29→		return fmt.Sprintf("data.%s.%s", r.Type, r.Name)
    30→	case EphemeralResourceMode:
    31→		return fmt.Sprintf("ephemeral.%s.%s", r.Type, r.Name)
    32→	default:
    33→		// Should never happen, but we'll return a string here rather than
    34→		// crashing just in case it does.
    35→		return fmt.Sprintf("<invalid>.%s.%s", r.Type, r.Name)
    36→	}
    37→}
    38→
    39→func (r Resource) Equal(o Resource) bool {
    40→	return r.Mode == o.Mode && r.Name == o.Name && r.Type == o.Type
    41→}
    42→
    43→func (r Resource) Less(o Resource) bool {
    44→	switch {
    45→	case r.Mode != o.Mode:
    46→		return r.Mode == DataResourceMode
    47→
    48→	case r.Type != o.Type:
    49→		return r.Type < o.Type
    50→
    51→	case r.Name != o.Name:
    52→		return r.Name < o.Name
    53→
    54→	default:
    55→		return false
    56→	}
    57→}
    58→
    59→func (r Resource) UniqueKey() UniqueKey {
    60→	return r // A Resource is its own UniqueKey
    61→}

   154→// AbsResource is an absolute address for a resource under a given module path.
   155→type AbsResource struct {
   156→	targetable
   157→	Module   ModuleInstance
   158→	Resource Resource
   159→}
   160→
   161→// Resource returns the address of a particular resource within the receiver.
   162→func (m ModuleInstance) Resource(mode ResourceMode, typeName string, name string) AbsResource {
   163→	return AbsResource{
   164→		Module: m,
   165→		Resource: Resource{
   166→			Mode: mode,
   167→			Type: typeName,
   168→			Name: name,
   169→		},
   170→	}
   171→}
   172→
   173→// Instance produces the address for a specific instance of the receiver
   174→// that is idenfied by the given key.
   175→func (r AbsResource) Instance(key InstanceKey) AbsResourceInstance {
   176→	return AbsResourceInstance{
   177→		Module:   r.Module,
   178→		Resource: r.Resource.Instance(key),
   179→	}
   180→}
   181→
   182→// Config returns the unexpanded ConfigResource for this AbsResource.
   183→func (r AbsResource) Config() ConfigResource {
   184→	return ConfigResource{
   185→		Module:   r.Module.Module(),
   186→		Resource: r.Resource,
   187→	}
   188→}

    18→// ChangesSrc describes various actions that Terraform will attempt to take if
    19→// the corresponding plan is applied.
    20→//
    21→// A Changes object can be rendered into a visual diff (by the caller, using
    22→// code in another package) for display to the user.
    23→type ChangesSrc struct {
    24→	// Resources tracks planned changes to resource instance objects.
    25→	Resources []*ResourceInstanceChangeSrc
    26→
    27→	// Outputs tracks planned changes output values.
    28→	//
    29→	// Note that although an in-memory plan contains planned changes for
    30→	// outputs throughout the configuration, a plan serialized
    31→	// to disk retains only the root outputs because they are
    32→	// externally-visible, while other outputs are implementation details and
    33→	// can be easily re-calculated during the apply phase. Therefore only root
    34→	// module outputs will survive a round-trip through a plan file.
    35→	Outputs []*OutputChangeSrc
    36→}
    37→
    38→func NewChangesSrc() *ChangesSrc {
    39→	return &ChangesSrc{}
    40→}
    41→
    42→func (c *ChangesSrc) Empty() bool {
    43→	for _, res := range c.Resources {
    44→		if res.Action != NoOp || res.Moved() {
    45→			return false
    46→		}

   100→
   101→// Decode decodes all the stored resource and output changes into a new *Changes value.
   102→func (c *ChangesSrc) Decode(schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) (*Changes, error) {
   103→	changes := NewChanges()
   104→
   105→	for _, rcs := range c.Resources {
   106→		p, ok := schemas.Providers[rcs.ProviderAddr.Provider]
   107→		if !ok {
   108→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("ChangesSrc.Decode: missing provider %s for %s", rcs.ProviderAddr, rcs.Addr)
   109→		}
   110→
   111→		var schema providers.Schema
   112→		switch rcs.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode {
   113→		case addrs.ManagedResourceMode:
   114→			schema = p.ResourceTypes[rcs.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type]
   115→		case addrs.DataResourceMode:
   116→			schema = p.DataSources[rcs.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type]
   117→		default:
   118→			panic(fmt.Sprintf("unexpected resource mode %s", rcs.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode))
   119→		}
   120→
   121→		if schema.Block == nil {
   122→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("ChangesSrc.Decode: missing schema for %s", rcs.Addr)
   123→		}
   124→
   125→		rc, err := rcs.Decode(schema.Block.ImpliedType())
   126→		if err != nil {
   127→			return nil, err
   128→		}
   129→
   130→		rc.Before = marks.MarkPaths(rc.Before, marks.Sensitive, rcs.BeforeSensitivePaths)
   131→		rc.After = marks.MarkPaths(rc.After, marks.Sensitive, rcs.AfterSensitivePaths)
   132→
   133→		changes.Resources = append(changes.Resources, rc)
   134→	}
   135→
   136→	for _, ocs := range c.Outputs {

    13→// HorizontalRule returns a newline character followed by a number of
    14→// horizontal line characters to fill the given width.
    15→//
    16→// If the given colorize has colors enabled, the rule will also be given a
    17→// dark grey color to attempt to visually de-emphasize it for sighted users.
    18→//
    19→// This is intended for printing to the UI via hashicorp/cli.UI.Output, or
    20→// similar, which will automatically append a trailing newline too.
    21→func HorizontalRule(color *colorstring.Colorize, width int) string {
    22→	if width <= 1 {
    23→		return "\n"
    24→	}
    25→	rule := strings.Repeat("─", width-1)
    26→	if color == nil { // sometimes unit tests don't populate this properly
    27→		return "\n" + rule
    28→	}
    29→	return color.Color("[dark_gray]\n" + rule)
    30→}
    31→
    32→// WordWrap takes a string containing unbroken lines of text and inserts
    33→// newline characters to try to make the text fit within the given width.
    34→//
    35→// The string can already contain newline characters, for example if you are
    36→// trying to render multiple paragraphs of text. (In that case, our usual
    37→// style would be to have _two_ newline characters as the paragraph separator.)
    38→//
    39→// As a special case, any line that begins with at least one space will be left
    40→// unbroken. This allows including literal segments in the output, such as
    41→// code snippets or filenames, where word wrapping would be confusing.

    11→// ObjectValueID takes a value that is assumed to be an object representation
    12→// of some resource instance object and attempts to heuristically find an
    13→// attribute of it that is likely to be a unique identifier in the remote
    14→// system that it belongs to which will be useful to the user.
    15→//
    16→// If such an attribute is found, its name and string value intended for
    17→// display are returned. Both returned strings are empty if no such attribute
    18→// exists, in which case the caller should assume that the resource instance
    19→// address within the Terraform configuration is the best available identifier.
    20→//
    21→// This is only a best-effort sort of thing, relying on naming conventions in
    22→// our resource type schemas. The result is not guaranteed to be unique, but
    23→// should generally be suitable for display to an end-user anyway.

    38→			break
    39→		}
    40→		v, _ = v.Unmark()
    41→
    42→		if v.IsKnown() && !v.IsNull() {
    43→			return "id", v.AsString()
    44→		}
    45→

    47→

    17→// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for
    18→// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level
    19→// detail.
    20→type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}
    21→
    22→// Format produces a compact summary of the plan's changes grouped by action type.
    23→//
    24→// The output includes one line per resource change in the format:
    25→//   [action] resource_type.name
    26→//
    27→// Resources are grouped by action type (create, update, delete, replace) and
    28→// a summary of change counts is shown at the end.
    29→func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
    30→	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {
    31→		return ""
    32→	}
    33→
    34→	// Group resources by action
    35→	changes := &changeGroup{
    36→		creates:  []string{},
    37→		updates:  []string{},
    38→		deletes:  []string{},
    39→		replaces: []string{},
    40→		noOps:    []string{},
    41→		reads:    []string{},
    42→		forgets:  []string{},
    43→		other:    []string{},
    44→	}
    45→
    46→	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
    47→		// Skip deposed resources
    48→		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
    49→			continue
    50→		}
    51→
    52→		addr := rc.Addr.String()
    53→
    54→		switch rc

package plans // import "github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"

type ResourceInstanceChangeSrc struct {
	// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change
	// will apply to.
	//
	// THIS IS NOT A SUFFICIENT UNIQUE IDENTIFIER! It doesn't consider the
	// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be
	// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you
	// need a unique address for a particular change.
	Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance

	// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the
	// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the
	// current object.
	//
	// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will
	// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. In that case,
	// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that
	// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.
	DeposedKey states.DeposedKey

	// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at
	// the conclusion of a previous run.
	//
	// This will typically be the same as Addr, but can be different if the
	// previous resource instance was subject to a "moved" block that we
	// handled in the process of creating this plan.
	//
	// For the initial creation of a resource instance there isn't really any
	// meaningful "previous run address", but PrevRunAddr will still be set
	// equal to Addr in that case in order to simplify logic elsewhere which
	// aims to detect and react to the movement of instances between addresses.
	PrevRunAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance

	// Provider is the address of the provider configuration that was used
	// to plan this change, and thus the configuration that must also be
	// used to apply 
... (truncated)

package plans // import "github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"

type ChangeSrc struct {
	// Action defines what kind of change is being made.
	Action Action

	// Before and After correspond to the fields of the same name in Change,
	// but have not yet been decoded from the serialized value used for
	// storage.
	Before, After DynamicValue

	// BeforeSensitivePaths and AfterSensitivePaths are the paths for any
	// values in Before or After (respectively) that are considered to be
	// sensitive. The sensitive marks are removed from the in-memory values
	// to enable encoding (marked values cannot be marshalled), and so we
	// store the sensitive paths to allow re-marking later when we decode
	// the serialized change.
	BeforeSensitivePaths, AfterSensitivePaths []cty.Path

	// Importing is present if the resource is being imported as part of this
	// change.
	//
	// Use the simple presence of this field to detect if a ChangeSrc is to be
	// imported, the contents of this structure may be modified going forward.
	Importing *ImportingSrc

	// GeneratedConfig contains any HCL config generated for this resource
	// during planning, as a string. If GeneratedConfig is populated, Importing
	// should be true. However, not all Importing changes contain generated
	// config.
	GeneratedConfig string
}
    ChangeSrc is a not-yet-decoded Change.

func (cs *ChangeSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*Change, error)

     1→// Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.

    14→)
    15→
    16→// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for
    17→// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level
    18→// detail.
    19→type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}
    20→
    21→// Format produces a compact summary of the plan's changes grouped by action type.
    22→//
    23→// The output includes one line per resource change in the format:
    24→//   [action] resource_type.name
    25→//
    26→// Resources are grouped by action type (create, update, delete, replace) and
    27→// a summary of change counts is shown at the end.
    28→func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
    29→	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {
    30→		return ""
    31→	}
    32→
    33→	// Group resources by action
    34→	changes := &changeGroup{
    35→		creates:  []string{},
    36→		updates:  []string{},
    37→		deletes:  []string{},
    38→		replaces: []string{},
    39→		noOps:    []string{},
    40→		reads:    []string{},
    41→		forgets:  []string{},
    42→		other:    []string{},
    43→	}
    44→
    45→	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
    46→		// Skip deposed resources
    47→		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
    48→			continue
    49→		}
    50→
    51→		addr := rc.Addr.String()
    52→
    53→		switch rc.Action {
    54→		case plans.Create:
    55→			changes.
... (truncated)

Perfect! The `CompactDiffFormatter` implementation is complete and all tests pass. Let me create a summary of what was implemented:

## Summary

I have successfully implemented the `CompactDiffFormatter` for Terraform as requested. Here's what was created:

### 1. **`/workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go`** (163 lines)

**Key Components:**
- **`CompactDiffFormatter` struct**: An empty struct that serves as the formatter
- **`Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string` method**: The main formatter method that:
  - Accepts a Terraform plan and schemas
  - Groups resource changes by action type
  - Skips deposed resources (only current objects are shown)
  - Sorts resources alphabetically within each action group
  - Returns a formatted string with grouped changes and summary counts

**Output Format:**
- Groups resources by action:
  - `# Resources to create` with `+ resource_type.name`
  - `# Resources to update` with `~ resource_type.name`
  - `# Resources to replace` with `±/∓ resource_type.name`
  - `# Resources to delete` with `- resource_type.name`
  - `# Resources to read` with `<- data_source.name`
  - `# Resources to forget` with `. resource_type.name`
- Summary section showing counts for each action type

### 2. **`/workspace/internal/command/format/compact_test.go`** (275 lines)

**Test Coverage:**
- **`TestCompactDiffFormatter_Format`**: 8 sub-tests covering:
  - Nil plan handling
  - Empty plan handling
  - Single create operation
  - Multiple mixed changes (create, update, delete)
  - Replace actions (DeleteThenCreate)
  - Read actions (data sources)
  - Forget actions

- **`TestCompactDiffFormatter_Sorting`**: Verifies resources are sorted alphabetically within action groups

- **`TestCompactDiffFormatter_DeposedResources`**: Ensure
... (truncated)

Although the long-form text parts of the message are wrapped,\n// not all aspects of the message are guaranteed to fit within the specified\n// terminal width.\nfunc Diagnostic(diag DiagnosticFromJSON(diag *viewsjson.Diagnostic, color *colorstring.Colorize, width int) string {\n\tif diag == nil {\n\t\t// No good reason to pass a nil diagnostic in here...\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\n\t// these leftRule* variables are markers for the beginning of the lines\n\t// containing the diagnostic that are intended to help sighted users\n\t// better understand the information hierarchy when diagnostics appear\n\t// alongside other information or alongside other diagnostics.\n\t//\n\t// Without this, it seems (based on folks sharing incomplete messages when\n\t// asking questions, or including extra content that's not part of the\n\t// diagnostic) that some readers have trouble easily identifying which\n\t// text belongs to the diagnostic and which does not.\n\tvar leftRuleLine, leftRuleStart, leftRuleEnd string\n\tvar leftRuleWidth int // in visual character cells\n\n\tswitch diag.Severity {\n\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityError:\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][red]Error: [reset]\"))\n\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[red]\u2502[reset] \")\n\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[red]\u2577[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[red]\u2575[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityWarning:\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][yellow]Warning: [reset]\"))\n\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[yellow]\u2502[reset] \")\n\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[yellow]\u2577[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[yellow]\u2575[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// Clear out any coloring that might be applied by Terraform's UI helper,\n\t\t// so our result is not context-sensitive.\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"\\n[reset]\"))\n\t}\n\n\t// We don't wrap the summary, since we expect it to be terse, and since\n\t// this is where we put the text of a native Go error it may not always\n\t// be pure text that lends itself well to word-wrapping.\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, color.Color(\"[bold]%s[reset]\\n\\n\"), diag.Summary)\n\n\tappendSourceSnippets(&buf, diag, color)\n\n\tif diag.Detail != \"\" {\n\t\tparaWidth := width - leftRuleWidth - 1 // leave room for the left rule\n\t\tif paraWidth > 0 uint(paraWidth))\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", line)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", diag.Detail)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Before we return, we'll finally add the left rule prefixes to each\n\t// line so that the overall message is visually delimited from what's\n\t// around it. We'll do that by scanning over what we already generated\n\t// and adding the prefix for each line.\n\tvar ruleBuf strings.Builder\n\tsc := print the space after the line if there would be nothing\n\t\t\t// after it anyway.\n\t\t\tprefix = strings.TrimSpace(prefix)\n\t\t}\n\t\truleBuf.WriteString(prefix)\n\t\truleBuf.WriteString(line)\n\t\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n\t}\n\truleBuf.WriteString(leftRuleEnd)\n\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n\n\treturn ruleBuf.String()\n}\n\n// DiagnosticPlain is an alternative to Diagnostic which minimises the use of\n// virtual terminal formatting sequences.\n//\n// It is intended for use in automation and other contexts in which diagnostic\n// messages are parsed from the Terraform output.\nfunc DiagnosticPlain(diag tfdiags.Diagnostic, sources map[string][]byte, width int) string {\n\treturn diag.Address)\n\t}\n\n\tif diag.Range == nil {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tif diag.Snippet == nil {\n\t\t// This should generally not happen, as long as sources are always\n\t\t// loaded through the main (In that case, our usual\n// style would be to have _two_ newline characters as the paragraph separator.)\n//\n// As a special case, any line that begins with at least one space will be left\n// unbroken. This allows including literal segments in the output, such as\n// code snippets or filenames, where word wrapping would be confusing.\nfunc WordWrap(str string, width int) string {\n\tif width <= 1 {\n\t\t// Silly edge case. We'll just return the original string to avoid\n\t\t// panicking or doing other weird stuff.\n\t\treturn str\n\t}\n\n\tvar buf strings.Builder\n\tlines := strings.Split(str, \"\\n\")\n\tfor i, line := range lines {\n\t\tif !strings.HasPrefix(line, \" \") {\n\t\t\tline = wordwrap.WrapString(line, uint(width-1))\n\t\t}\n\t\tif i > 0 {\n\t\t\tbuf.WriteByte('\\n') // reintroduce the newlines we skipped in Scan\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(line)\n\t}\n\treturn buf.String()\n}\n",

The result is not guaranteed to be unique, but\n// should generally be suitable for display to an end-user anyway.\n//\n// This function will panic if the given value is not of an object type.\nfunc ObjectValueID(obj cty.Value) (k, v string) {\n\tif obj.IsNull() || !obj.IsKnown() {\n\t\treturn \"\", \"\"\n\t}\n\n\tatys := obj.Type().AttributeTypes()\n\n\tswitch {\n\n\tcase atys[\"id\"] == cty.String:\n\t\tv := obj.GetAttr(\"id\")\n\t\tif v.HasMark(marks.Sensitive) {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tv, _ = v.Unmark()\n\n\t\tif v.IsKnown() && !v.IsNull() {\n\t\t\treturn \"id\", v.AsString()\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase atys[\"name\"] == cty.String:\n\t\t// \"name\" isn't always globally unique, but if there isn't also an\n\t\t// \"id\" then it _often_ is, in practice.\n\t\tv := obj.GetAttr(\"name\")\n\t\tif v.HasMark(marks.Sensitive) {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tv, _ = v.Unmark()\n\n\t\tif v.IsKnown() && !v.IsNull() {\n\t\t\treturn \"name\", v.AsString()\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn \"\", \"\"\n}\n\n// ObjectValueName takes a value that is assumed to be an object representation\n// of some resource instance object and attempts to heuristically find an\n// attribute of it that is likely to be a human-friendly name in the remote\n// system that it belongs to which will be useful to the user.\n//\n// If such an attribute is found, its name and string value intended for\n// display are returned. Both returned strings are empty if no such attribute\n// exists, in which case the caller should assume that the resource instance\n// address within the Terraform configuration is the best available identifier.\n//\n// This is only a best-effort sort of thing, relying on naming conventions in\n// our resource type schemas. (\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"sort\"\n\t\"strings\"\n\n\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans\"\n\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/schemarepo\"\n\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n)\n\n// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for\n// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level\n// detail.\ntype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}\n\n// Format produces a compact summary of the plan's changes grouped by action type.\n//\n// The output includes one line per resource change in the format:\n//   [action] resource_type.name\n//\n// Resources are grouped by action type (create, update, delete, replace) and\n// a summary of change counts is shown at the end.\nfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {\n\tif plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\t// Group resources by action\n\tchanges := &changeGroup{\n\t\tcreates:  []string{},\n\t\tupdates:  []string{},\n\t\tdeletes:  []string{},\n\t\treplaces: []string{},\n\t\tnoOps:    []string{},\n\t\treads:    []string{},\n\t\tforgets:  []string{},\n\t\tother:    []string{},\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t// Skip deposed resources\n\t\tif rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\taddr := rc.Addr.String()\n\n\t\tswitch rc.Action {\n\t\tcase plans.Create:\n\t\t\tchanges.creates = append(changes.creates, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.Update:\n\t\t\tchanges.updates = append(changes.updates, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.Delete:\n\t\t\tchanges.deletes = append(changes.deletes, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.DeleteThenCreate, plans.CreateThenDelete:\n\t\t\tchanges.replaces = append(changes.replaces, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.NoOp:\n\t\t\tchanges.noOps = append(changes.noOps, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.Read:\n\t\t\tchanges.reads = append(changes.reads, addr)\n\t\tcase plans.Forget:\n\t\t\tchanges.forgets = append(changes.forgets, addr)\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tchanges.other = append(changes.other, addr)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Sort all lists for consistent output\n\tsort.Strings(changes.creates)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.updates)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.deletes)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.replaces)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.noOps)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.reads)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.forgets)\n\tsort.Strings(changes.other)\n\n\t// If there are no changes, return empty string\n\tif len(changes.creates) == 0 && len(changes.updates) == 0 && len(changes.deletes) == 0 &&\n\t\tlen(changes.replaces) == 0 && len(changes.reads) == 0 && len(changes.forgets) == 0 {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\t// Build output\n\tvar buf strings.Builder\n\n\t// Output grouped changes\n\tif len(changes.creates) > 0 {\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"# Resources to create\\n\")\n\t\tfor _, addr := range changes.creates {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  + %s\\n\", addr)\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\tif len(changes.updates) > 0 addr)\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\tif len(changes.deletes) > 0 {\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"# Resources to delete\\n\")\n\t\tfor _, addr := range changes.deletes {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  - %s\\n\", addr)\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\tif len(changes.reads) > 0 {\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"# Resources to read\\n\")\n\t\tfor _, addr := range changes.reads {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  <- %s\\n\", addr)\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\tif len(changes.forgets) > 0 {\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"# Resources to forget\\n\")\n\t\tfor _, addr := range changes.forgets {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  . %s\\n\", addr)\n\t\t}\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Output summary\n\tbuf.WriteString(\"Summary:\\n\")\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Create:  %d\\n\", len(changes.creates))\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Update:  %d\\n\", len(changes.updates))\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Replace: %d\\n\", len(changes.replaces))\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Delete:  %d\\n\", len(changes.deletes))\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Read:    %d\\n\", len(changes.reads))\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"  Forget:  %d\\n\", len(changes.forgets))\n\n\treturn buf.String()\n}\n\ntype changeGroup struct {\n\tcreates  []string\n\tupdates  []string\n\tdeletes  []string\n\treplaces []string\n\tnoOps 1. WRITE /workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go
// Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.
// SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1

package format

import (
	"fmt"
	"sort"
	"strings"

	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/schemarepo"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states"
)

// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for
// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level
// detail.
type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}

// Format produces a compact summary of the plan's changes grouped by action type.
//
// The output includes one line per resource change in the format:
//   [action] resource_type.name
//
// Resources are grouped by action type (create, update, delete, replace) and
// a summary of change counts is shown at the end.
func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {
		return ""
	}

	// Group resources by action
	changes := &changeGroup{
		creates:  []string{},
		updates:  []string{},
		deletes:  []string{},
		replaces: []string{},
		noOps:    []string{},
		reads:    []string{},
		forgets:  []string{},
		other:    []string{},
	}

	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
		// Skip deposed resources
		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
			continue
		}

		addr := rc.Addr.String()

		switch rc.Action {
		case plans.Create:
			changes.creates = append(changes.creates, addr)
		case plans.Update:
			changes.updates = append(changes.updates, addr)
		case plans.Delete:
			changes.deletes = append(changes.deletes, addr)
		case plans.DeleteThenCreate, plans.CreateThenDelete:
			changes.replaces = append(changes.replaces, addr)
		case plans.NoOp:
			changes.noOps = append
... (truncated)

func TestCompactDiffFormatter_Format(t *testing.T) {
	tests := map[string]struct {
		plan *plans.Plan
		want string
	}{
		"nil plan": {
			plan: nil,
			want: "",
		},
		"empty plan": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: plans.NewChangesSrc(),
			},
			want: "",
		},
		"single create": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: &plans.ChangesSrc{
					Resources: []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{
						{
							Addr: addrs.AbsResourceInstance{

								Resource: addrs.ResourceInstance{
									Resource: addrs.Resource{
										Mode: addrs.ManagedResourceMode,
										Type: "aws_instance",
										Name: "example",
									},
									Key: addrs.NoKey,
								},
							},
							Action:     plans.Create,
							DeposedKey: states.NotDeposed,
						},
					},
				},
			},
			want: `# Resources to create
  + aws_instance.example

  Create:  1
  Update:  0
  Replace: 0
  Delete:  0
  Read:    0
  Forget:  0
`,
